Today most of society would consider the turkey an unintelligent bird and they do not have an understanding of how loving, wise and fearless the turkey really is or what they symbolized to our ancestors.  There was once a strong connection and understanding of the turkey, so much that some tribes had Turkey Clans; the Shawnee, Miami, Delaware and Zuni, just to name a few. In the Pima tribe, the turkey is considered a rain spirit.  Turkeys have knowledge of and can predict the weather. They love their relatives so much that they would sacrifice their own life to protect the others.\nWhen the Dog Soldier Warrior Society was given to the people, they wore turkey feathers as a sign that their love for the people and their fearlessness to protect the people was as true as the turkey. Only the bravest of men were brought into this warrior society.  Those warriors admired the turkey so much that they fashioned their style of fighting after the turkey.   A Dog Soldier was the first line of defense for the people. They would ride towards and dismount or run out on foot to meet the cavalry soldiers and run a stake or lance through the leather that tailed from their headdress or waist. There were only three ways that the warrior could be set free: if he survived the battle, if another Dog Soldier cut him free or death.  Just as we had brave warriors on horseback, we also had brave warriors on the ground.  Like the Wanbli (Eagle) of the air, there is the Waglekšun (turkey) on the ground.\nSo you see, the turkey meant more to the people than just a meal. They were just as meaningful as the Eagle. We admired all of creation because they taught us how to be connected to the Creator and the earth. The Waglekšun (turkey) was one of many teachers of love, protection and fearlessness.                    \n\n                               - Mo Brings Being there for 6 years with my grandparents was great because I feel like I really got to know them. My grandfather passed away last year, but at least I knew who he was. We were buddies, like we’d watch cricket together, eat together.\" The communication barrier: \"I can understand Telegu but it could be hard to talk to my grandparents, like the conversation was superficial. But being there and just seeing their movements and lives helped me understand them better. A lot of people don't get to know their grandparents but I’m glad I did. Moving was so hard because all my best friends were here, but it was easy to adapt to new situations I think. When you’re in 7th grade you adapt to a new environment. I just switched phases. No one here would even know unless I tell them. \" \"In America we’d go to temple, we’d always celebrate festivals. I feel like I’m already so secure with myself culturally – ISA was for the friend group. I thought it would be really cool to join a family. My favorite part about being Indian is the food.
